                   President of the World Peace Unification Family, Hwang Seon-jo

1)  
Heaven's Heart Towards Elijah  
1 Kings 19:1-21  
<Prayer (I)> Today, as we gather before Your presence, kneeling in concern for our inadequacies, please allow us to gain insight into where our hearts may be.  
We know that the path You have paved for the way of life has been a most solemn and sanctified journey.  
Father, please have compassion on Your sons and daughters gathered here. Reveal Your dignified presence among us, establish the standard of victory You have permitted, and recognize us as a sanctified group, we earnestly hope and desire this.  
If the remaining providential path is a path of sorrow, we understand that the responsibility to overcome this sorrow lies with us, and we also know that those who cannot feel Heaven's infinite sorrow cannot take responsibility for that sorrow. We are aware that we must take responsibility for Heaven's sorrowful heart and the struggles that remain, so please allow us to be those who can take on the sorrowful heart and battles of Heaven.  
We know that to carry out this work, we must experience greater sorrow than anyone else, and we must not become casualties in the battlefield of injustice.  
Father, may our bodies become victorious offerings dedicated before Heaven on March 15, 1959, at the former headquarters church (Cheongpa-dong 1-ga).  
8   Heaven's Heart Towards Elijah  
Please allow us to be a gathering that attends this time with a heart of concern.  
Although two thousand years have passed since Jesus came, the true victory altar that Heaven wept over while Jesus was on the Mount of Golgotha has not yet appeared on this earth. It is time for a global Golgotha, where Heaven cannot remain still, and where humanity on earth cannot remain still, to manifest, and it is time for the Mount of Gethsemane to appear. We must have many saints who can take on this responsibility. However, the more we realize that there is no group that can come before Heaven and rejoice, the more we understand that the sons and daughters who are concerned about the Father's heart cannot help but lament over this reality.  
Father! The more Your earnest heart longs for a day of hope, the greater the heart that longs for a faithful appearance on this earth.  
Today, may we offer all our hearts and bodies so that we may be held in Your hands and established in Your heart, allowing us to bear the historical sorrows.  
We know that this time must be one of renewal and resurrection for our hearts and bodies through the work that You personally carry out. Please forgive us for not fulfilling the responsibilities entrusted to us over the past week, forgive us for not being faithful before You, forgive us for not holding onto Your heart and living a tearful life, and forgive us for forgetting that You did not hesitate to take the arduous steps to find each of us.  
At this time, may we make new resolutions and new determinations, realizing all our past inadequacies, and may we be sons and daughters who can hold onto our hearts centered on Your heart and step forward. Father, we earnestly hope and desire this.  
Father, this day is a holy day, so please have compassion on the thirty million people in a pitiful situation. Be their friend, be their leader, and be the Lord who resurrects their lives, we earnestly hope and desire this.  
May You be the center of their hopes. Allow them to be a group that cannot move without You, allow them to be a nation, and allow them to become a denomination, we hope and desire this, Father.  
We earnestly hope and desire that the blessings You will grant to this nation may be poured out through this time. Please allow Your sons and daughters who bear the responsibility for a day of victory to fulfill that mission and responsibility. We know that the responsibility to fulfill this will and reveal Your glory lies with this nation. We understand that there are infinite trials in the process of fulfilling that responsibility, so we earnestly hope and desire that we may be sons and daughters who can fulfill our responsibilities and stand in Your place even amidst those trials.  
Please bless the countless people who do not know this will. In this time when the waves of life and death are sweeping away, please allow many to emerge among humanity who can hold onto You and become Your sons and daughters.  
Please allow many sons and daughters to emerge among the people of this earth who can stand before You and bear the overall responsibility to protect humanity from the whip of judgment. We earnestly hope and desire this, Father.  
If there are those who do not know such a mission, such a time, and such a responsibility, please warn them through us and allow them to become sons and daughters who can fulfill the responsibilities and missions of the end times. We earnestly hope and desire this, Father.  
Bless this day. Please extend Your hand of grace uniformly over those who are spread out in the regions, bearing lonely hearts and appealing before You, and do not let them fall away in the midst of the struggle to establish the day of victory You have permitted. We earnestly hope and desire this, Father.  
At this time, from the beginning to the end, Father, please preside over us personally and do not let this time become one where the powers of darkness move. We earnestly ask and desire this.  
We offer everything before You, so please take charge of it. We pray in Your name. Amen.  
<Prayer (II)> We know that many people on this earth have walked the path of labor for the sake of Your will and have gone through bloody battles of tears.  
Today, we know that we must become the fruit of that blood before Heaven and that we must raise the flag of victory on the foundation of the remaining providence.  
In this one hour today, please do not let us become those who think of ourselves as our own. Our hearts are not ours, our lives that are moving are not ours, and our desires that we hope for are not ours, so please allow us not to approach Heaven with a heart that counts based on ourselves. We are those who began with You, Father, so please allow this hour to be one where we can only move as Yours, we earnestly hope and desire this.  
Our hearts must become Yours, our bodies must become Yours, and our claims must become Yours, so please do not allow anything that is not Yours. If there are elements of evil in our hearts and bodies that You do not desire, please remove them, and remove all claims that are not Yours, so that this hour may only be one where we can move as Yours, Father, we earnestly hope and desire this.  
No matter how capable someone may be on this earth, who can stand before Heaven? When we think about the fact that no one can appear before You with conditions for excuses, we are those who must repent in our hearts, we are those who are soaked in the history of sin, and we are those who have become offerings for Satan upon historical sins. We know that it is time to realize this.  
Father, our hearts must become Yours, and our bodies must become Yours, yet we know that we have become offerings for Satan, so please restore a heart that can mourn this and raise a heart of repentance that can feel this deeply. Please allow us to realize ourselves and discover ourselves so that we can establish a connection with Heaven, we earnestly hope and desire this, Father.  
We know that countless Satans are targeting our hearts and bodies. If there are bitter roots of sin that You cannot tolerate, Father! Please appear and raise a work of recreation with the authority of power, and let our hearts be able to surrender before You through the work of Heaven, we earnestly hope and desire this, Father.  
When Heaven moves, the earth cannot remain still, and when the earth demands from Heaven, Heaven cannot but fulfill it. We know this. Are there sons and daughters of Heaven who are fighting with true hearts to hold onto Heaven as their own? Are there those who know Heaven's circumstances as their own, who know Heaven's work as their work, who know Heaven's ideals as their ideals, and who fight to hold onto this, who endure ridicule for this, and who live their lives for this? If we cannot say that we are in such a position, please allow us to confess that we are sinners who cannot be accepted before Heaven.  
Today, we do not know, but Heaven has sent many prophets and sages over the long span of six thousand years to build altars of blood, and has sent loyal martyrs to guide the direction of this nation. Please do not let us forget that there has been Your effort to internally govern beyond any region and across any nation.  
You have poured all Your heart into fulfilling this one will, You have made every effort, and You have been prepared for any sacrifice to find us, so please do not let us become shameless sons and daughters who cannot stand before Your grace, we earnestly hope and desire this, Father.  
Now we know that Heaven exists, and we know who the Heavenly Father is.  
We know that there are inevitable conditions for us to establish a relationship with You, Father, so please allow us to establish a connection with the Heavenly Father through such hearts today, allowing us to feel Your sorrow as our sorrow, and Your lament and sadness as our lament and sadness. Please allow a heavenly march to emerge before this nation to engage in battle against Satan, and please allow it to manifest on this earth.  
Please allow us to drive out the enemy Satan who has slandered Heaven for six thousand years from this earth, and allow us to quickly build the ideal garden where You can fulfill Your grievances, we earnestly hope and desire this, Father.  
Father, please guide the direction that the nation must go, illuminate the path that the denomination must take, and clarify the way that true sons and daughters must follow. We know that the time of historical sorrow has come, where chaos and confusion are taking hold of the powers of darkness, so please establish a standard that can overcome this time, we earnestly hope and desire this, Father.  
We know that there has been no time without sorrow for Jesus and God who have come to humanity. Looking back at Jesus two thousand years ago, we know that He shed tears that no one knew about, lived in hunger that no one knew about, and wept sorrowfully in the path of persecution that no one knew about.  
We know that Jesus walked such a path, and that countless saints who followed Him also walked the path of blood and fought without concern for death.  
The time is approaching when we must offer living sacrifices to Heaven and receive blessings, and the time is coming when we must sing of Heaven's glory with all our lives, but where are Your sons and daughters who will offer living sacrifices before You? Where are those who can please You and offer praises in glory? We know the heart of the Father who is searching for such figures. If there is sorrow, it is because He has not found His counterpart, and it is because He has not found the embodiment of glory. We hope that we may have a trembling heart that fears that such heavenly sorrow may be passed down to future generations through our footsteps today, Father, please forgive us.  
Your sons and daughters gathered here, what do you hope for as you have come? What will you accomplish? The place you must go is not this place, but the house of the Father. The place you must stay is the center of the Father's heart. Is there anyone seated on the throne of the Father? Is there anyone who will be remembered in the Father's heart? If we cannot become such figures, we know that we will only be the ridicule and offerings of countless Satans. Please allow us to be those who can bow down before the Father with one heart at this time.  
The path to the heavenly nature is the path of the cross. Therefore, we must carry our own crosses to the summit of Golgotha, and we must advance to the place where the blood of the cross was shed and endure persecution. Please let us know that Heaven is searching for a group that will give their all to walk this Golgotha path, forgetting themselves, their sorrows, and their pains, we earnestly hope and desire this, Father.  
Please have compassion on the thirty million people of Korea, and bless the many denominations that have appeared on behalf of the nation. This is a time when brothers are biting each other, where family members have become enemies, violating heavenly principles and destroying human relationships. This is a time when those who call upon Heaven are also being mocked and devoured by those who call upon Heaven, and those who understand the sorrow of Heaven must lament and sigh during this time. Please have compassion on this pitiful nation that does not understand this, Father.
If one were to search for the true path, it is a path that cannot be traveled without tears. If one were to seek the true way to live, it is a path that must be pursued day and night without hesitation. However, the thirty million people of this nation do not know this. Who is responsible for their fate, and who can empathize with the sorrow of heaven on their behalf? There is no one to take responsibility for their fate, no one to alleviate the sorrow of heaven, and no one to hear the sounds of heaven's lament and cries. If such a person were to arise, the sorrow of heaven would not penetrate the earth, and the judgment of heaven would not fall upon the land.

Heaven's Heart Toward Elijah
Father, please allow us to understand the sorrow of Jesus, who expressed His sadness in this age. It is not necessary to know Jesus only as the historical figure; it is time for us to know the present Jesus within our circumstances. Before that high and noble heart, before that love, may we offer our bodies and minds as a sacrifice, and may we become a group that cries out toward heaven, whether we live or die. This group will be those who are marginalized on this earth and those who are forsaken before the denominations. We hope and desire that your sons and daughters gathered here may become a group that can defend such a position.

Father, please let us know that the sorrow of heaven remains before this nation, a sorrow that we cannot forget even if we try. We are those who love our own comfort. We are a pitiful group that does not know that before enjoying our own comfort, there is the sorrow of heaven, and that the battle of heaven has already begun before we even fight for ourselves.

What is the purpose of our coming here today? We did not come to meet any particular person. We did not come to make friends, nor did we come to meet any learned individuals; we came solely to meet the Father, to understand the sorrow of the Father, and to bear the Father's cross. Those who dislike this, O Father! Please remove them from here, and separate those who cannot take responsibility for this work. We earnestly hope and desire that we may become sons and daughters who can shoot arrows at Satan to protect the final stronghold and be willing to fall for heaven.

Those who have come seeking the path that others do not walk must not only empathize with the sorrows unknown to others but also live a life that others do not know. Father, if you have made their circumstances thus, please take responsibility for them, and if you have created their environment in this way, please take responsibility for that environment as well. The Father who takes responsibility has not changed, but may we be those who can see that you are sighing as you observe our changing appearances.

Heaven's heart has manifested as one heart, establishing a standard of heart to unify four thousand years of history. However, because humans have violated and betrayed it, humanity today is in a tragic state. Father, please turn back the countless people on this earth who do not know that their sorrow is your sorrow.

Please allow us to be a lonely group that can shed tears and build altars for them. Jacob built an altar of sorrow during his journey in the wilderness, as did Moses and Elijah. We know that none of our ancestors, who bore the will of heaven, walked a path without such experiences. We wish to inherit their tradition, so please allow us to build the altars that remain and to rebuild the fallen walls, preparing the holy place for the Father, so that we may be sons and daughters who can serve you, O Father.

On this day, Father, is there a blessing that you will grant? Please bless us. If not, please allow us to empathize with your sorrow. Thus, we earnestly hope and desire that you will raise a heart that can expose its sins and repent.

Father, please be concerned about the path the Korean church is taking, and take charge of all of them. Please recognize the circumstances of those who are being marginalized, and acknowledge those who are being chased and lamenting. We earnestly hope and desire that you will grant them a day of ultimate victory where they can be embraced in the arms of your love. Even as they struggle through the processes they must overcome, please grant a new morning of light to the countless people who are steadily walking forward.

To your sons and daughters gathered here today, if they have not been faithful before you, may they bow their heads and enter into your heart with a fervent heart filled with admiration and longing. May this time allow them to enter into the realm of heart where they can call you Father beyond the limits of their understanding, and may it be a time to establish a connection with your grace of mercy.

Heaven's Heart Toward Elijah
We earnestly hope and desire that you will embrace the lonely family members scattered across the regions with the same grace at this time. I pray all these words in your name. Amen.

<Word> After the history of the fall began, God, without regard for the countless efforts over a long period, held onto the chosen Israel and, after three thousand years, established King Saul with great hope and expectation, even though the Israelite nation at that time did not know. However, because Saul could not bear the responsibility, God's original intention was extended through King David to King Solomon. In other words, the will of God that was to be fulfilled through Saul was extended for 120 years until the time of King Solomon.

The Jewish people, who were divided and served foreign gods
King Solomon had the heavenly responsibility to build the temple and lead his nation to unite with the temple, yet he could not fulfill that mission and, by committing sins himself, allowed the nation to be mocked by Satan.

Ultimately, after the death of King Solomon, Israel (the northern kingdom) and Judah (the southern kingdom) were divided by King Jeroboam and King Rehoboam. The chosen Israelite nation, which should have followed one leader centered on God, who would go left when he went left and right when he went right, was led by God through the history of labor but, contrary to heaven's hope, was divided into two dynasties of the north and south. We know well the sorrowful fact that the entire twelve tribes of Israel should have stood on heaven's side and united as one around one altar.

When Jacob was heading toward Haran, God appeared to him at Bethel and blessed him, and Jacob set up a pillar with the stone he had been sleeping on and made a vow to God. And before crossing the Jabbok River, he made a heap of stones on Mount Gilead and made a promise to Laban in the name of God. Thus, blessed from heaven, the Israelite nation that began with Jacob was to be one sovereign nation where God could exercise authority, and as a sovereign people, they were to uphold the temple. However, they forsook that heavenly mission and the twelve tribes were divided into ten tribes in the north and two tribes in the south. We must not understand this sorrowful fact merely as a historical fact.

At that time, the Israelite nation was a remnant that had survived through the three thousand years of God's tearful history and the path of struggle, a remnant that had been marginalized, a remnant that had remained in a sorrowful path of being despised. They forgot their position to resent and oppose the many foreign nations that had violated their ancestors and the numerous Satans that had betrayed God's will, and instead engaged in bloody battles among themselves. We must think about what God's heart must have felt as He looked upon the sorrowful state of Israel and Judah, who disregarded such sorrowful facts.

The Israelite nation, led by Joshua and Caleb into the land of Canaan, was to build the temple where God would dwell centered on King Solomon. Yet, they quarreled with each other after being divided into the northern kingdom of Israel and the southern kingdom of Judah, even worshiping Baal and Asherah. We must understand God's heart as He looked upon such a tragic scene.

The God who led this history became deeply sorrowful, and that profound sorrow has continued through history to us today. But where has that historical sorrow gone, where has the national sorrow gone, and furthermore, where has the heavenly sorrow gone? We did not know that these conditions surrounded our hearts, that these conditions enveloped our surroundings as we sought heaven, and that these conditions were trying to correct our direction beyond our conscious world.

The Heart of the Called Elijah
As God looked upon such a tragic environment, He found and raised a man named Elijah among the farmers living in Gilead. There were kings of Israel and chiefs of the ten tribes, yet He chose Elijah, who was merely living as a farmer in Gilead. You must understand this sad fact.

The king of Israel, who was to govern the nation and lead it through the heavenly temple, forgot that responsibility and rejected and resented heaven while violating the nation. Furthermore, he built altars for Baal, the enemy of heaven, and made Asherah poles to present before the nation and worship them. We must consider how much God must have hated King Ahab. God could not suppress that feeling of hatred and could not restrain the sorrowful heart that had to witness His chosen people being violated by Satan. Therefore, He chose one person to resolve that sorrowful situation and heart. However, that chosen person was not a king, nor a royal, nor any chief, but the commoner Elijah.

Heaven could not find what it was seeking, could not possess what it should have, and stood in a position where it could not lead those it should have led. With a sorrowful heart, it sought the kings, chiefs, and many people, but could not find them. Instead, it raised one person who understood the national sorrow and heavenly sorrow of that era, who prayed and cried out to heaven, and that person was Elijah.

Thus, Elijah was raised. Everyone! Recall that Elijah. Elijah was not someone supported by his tribe, nor did he have an environment that defended his position and situation. He was someone who understood the heart of heaven and appeared in response to heaven's call.

At that time, the environment he faced and looked upon was the enemy's environment under the sovereignty of King Ahab. In such an environment, Elijah, who was called by heaven, had a stronger determination than anyone else to hold onto this nation, even if it meant his death. Even if he died, he wanted to respect the tradition of the prophetic ancestors who had represented the historical heart in the providential history of the nation. Furthermore, he was someone who shed tears for the nation and history, and you must remember that he was Elijah who cried for them. That is why heaven sought such an Elijah.

Therefore, the title I want to speak to you about today is "Heaven's Heart Toward Elijah." I will briefly share on this topic.

Look. God found Elijah to represent the sorrowful heart of over three thousand years. In other words, He did not forget the promise to bless Israel by raising His hand, which was felt by many prophetic ancestors who walked through history, and He held onto the heart that had been providentially guided through the historical process of over a thousand years from Jacob to the time of Elijah.

We cannot help but think that there was a sorrowful yet hopeful aspect for God when He raised Elijah to restore the Israelite nation, which had been captured by the enemy. When God saw the chosen Israelite nation worshiping the foreign god Baal along with King Ahab and his queen Jezebel, and being defiled by the Asherah idols, He could not bear the sorrow and called Elijah. However, Elijah could not appear before the Father with a joyful heart.

Elijah did not say, "Father! Yes, I will go the way you desire. I will take responsibility for your calling." Instead, he said, "I am nothing but a commoner. O God, there are many great chiefs, kings, and royals, and countless Israelites. What is it that you have sought someone as insignificant as me?" The conscience of Elijah was such that the greater his concern for Israel, the more he could not refuse before heaven without selfishness.

However, heaven knew that it could not raise the entire nation at that time and that it had to raise Elijah. Therefore, God did not command Elijah to fulfill that mission immediately, but rather organized the environment and gave various shocks so that he could appear automatically.

Thus, when Elijah received the call from heaven and appeared before King Ahab, heaven did not make him decide instantly, saying, "This is the command of the Father, so I will do it right away." Instead, He allowed him to encounter an environment where he could not go even if he wanted to go, and made him aware of his own misery and the nation's misery, leading him to the resolution that he would die for the nation and die for his tribe, and only then did he raise him as the responsible leader.

The Faith Posture of Noah and Mary
Our ancestor Noah was also like this. When God said, "In 120 years, I will judge the whole world with water; you shall build an ark," Noah must have had many moments of doubt in his internal struggle and found himself in situations where he could lament his own weakness. However, the more he stood in such a position, the more he felt deeply that the day was approaching when humanity on this earth would be swept away by the judgment of water.

Now let us look at Mary. She was a pure virgin and the true woman of Israel who cared deeply for the Israelite nation. She was the one who had the strongest heart among the Israelites, longing for the Messiah, our leader, whom heaven had promised thousands of years ago. Mary understood the heart of heaven that was sending the Messiah. Although humanity did not understand the heart of Mary, who represented the Israelite nation that was to welcome the Messiah, heaven did.

Mary possessed this emotional standard. However, her emotional standard was not to rise up as a warrior to crush the enemy on behalf of her nation. She did not intend to become a warrior to resolve the sorrows of her nation that was groaning in pain. She had the heart that could shed tears, knowing that there was sorrow in heaven, a heart that understood that there was a historical path of sorrow behind the nation that people at that time did not know, and a heart that lamented the pitiful reality of the chosen Israelite nation that could not stand before God.

When such a noble figure did not appear, she shed tears, hoping that the figure would appear, and because she bore a heart that was deeply rooted in sorrow, she was able to connect with the historical heart of heaven. Thus, unexpectedly, at that time, the angel appeared and said, "You will conceive and bear a son..." (Luke)
1:31) was a message that struck like a bolt from the blue. However, Mary hesitated and said, "How can this be, since I do not know a man?" (Luke 1:34). The angel replied, "For with God nothing will be impossible." (Luke 1:37). Hearing these words from the angel, who wished to fulfill the will of the Father, Mary did not hesitate and said, "I am the Lord's servant; may your word to me be fulfilled." 

Thus, Mary's heart, which sought to connect with the heart of heaven, was earnest. She found herself in a position where her life could be shattered, and she might ultimately face death, yet she said, "May your will be done." This was because if the word spread that she was conceived as a virgin, she would be stoned to death immediately according to Moses' law, be expelled from her nation, and be rejected by her people. In such an environment, no one among the people of Israel would welcome her, but Mary still said, "Lord! I am your servant; may your will be done."

From the depths of her sorrowful heart and her practical faith, Mary became the historical protagonist, the protagonist of her time, the protagonist of the future, and the mother who could give birth to the Messiah, the protagonist of all humanity.

Elijah's Tears and Loyalty
In a similar manner, Elijah was called before heaven. Until heaven sought him, Elijah was a prince of tears, shedding tears that no one else knew about. He was a prince of tears who shed more tears than any king of Israel or any person in Israel. Even if there were Israelites who shed tears in their pitiful state, their tears were for themselves, but the tears that Elijah shed, though he was a commoner, transcended himself. You must understand that he had a heart that questioned why Israel had come to such a state, led by heaven.

After 400 years of suffering in Egypt and losing 600,000 people during the 40 years in the wilderness, the nation that entered the land of Canaan and established a nation saw its chosen people, the Israelites, suffer such humiliation at the hands of foreign nations, and Elijah was filled with deep sorrow witnessing the downfall of God's chosen people. He prayed fervently for his nation and devoted himself to heaven more than anyone else. It was because of such Elijah that heaven sought him to represent Israel.

When Elijah was called before heaven and heard the words, "Elijah, Elijah!" he must have been bewildered. He might have thought, "Is this for me? This is something I never even dreamed of, something unexpected." As he stood before such a great purpose, heaven said, "I am with you; go and advise King Ahab." In response to that command from heaven, Elijah fought against King Ahab on behalf of heaven.

Elijah, who feared that the day of judgment would soon come due to the Baal and Asherah idols brought in by the foreign queen Jezebel, and who had mourned for many years with the sorrow of heaven and his nation, stepped forward saying, "Father, if the nation can be saved, let me be the sacrifice to carry out this task." After receiving such a command from heaven, from the day he set out toward King Ahab, there was no joy in Elijah's life. He had to witness unexpected phenomena, hear things he never imagined, and live in uncomfortable conditions for eating, dressing, and sleeping.

Elijah warned King Ahab that if he worshiped foreign gods, he would perish and that famine would come, but Ahab did not listen to him and instead sought to kill Elijah. So, Elijah fled to the brook Cherith. At that time, Elijah's heart was also filled with infinite sorrow.

Had he not known heaven, he might have had a house to lie down in, parents, relatives, and siblings. He might have had land to live on and an environment that recognized him, but from the day he held onto heaven, he found himself in a situation he never expected, hiding in a valley.

Still, Elijah did not blame heaven; he blamed Ahab, and he did not blame the nation; he blamed Jezebel. If he had not had a loyal heart toward heaven in such a pursued and oppressed environment, Elijah would have abandoned that situation. However, the tighter his circumstances became, the more he held onto the sorrow of heaven and the nation. Elijah, knowing that a life of mourning for heaven was greater than a moment of joy, did not forsake the achievements of historical ancestors and disregarded his own suffering to draw closer and closer to heaven.

Yet, Elijah did not realize that as much as his brothers cared for him, heaven cared for him even more; as much as his relatives worried about him, heaven worried about him even more; and as much as his parents were concerned for him, heaven was concerned for him even more. It was only after time had passed that he came to understand the heart of heaven, which is a sorrowful circumstance in seeking heaven.

Elijah's Significant Acts and Sufferings
Even in the environment of hiding at the brook Cherith, Elijah renewed his resolve. Although people did not understand the painful heart of Elijah, who was hiding to defeat Ahab and Jezebel and save the nation of Israel, ravens came and brought him food. You must understand that even while continuing a life of hunger, Elijah vowed to seek those who could understand the heart of heaven.

Elijah was filled with the sorrow of heaven for a nation standing at the crossroads of life and death, and he knew that the day of judgment was approaching due to that sorrowful heart. The more he felt that he could not bear it alone, the more he longed for a comrade who could sacrifice himself for the will of heaven. Elijah, who loved his nation, wanted to love the comrades who appeared before him as much as he loved heaven.

Such a heart of Elijah was a heart that could save the nation and encompass those who could save the nation. It was also a heartfelt desire to connect heaven and humanity. Because Elijah had such feelings, heaven chose him and guided him.

Once, when the hungry Elijah was led by heaven to the house of the widow of Zarephath to eat bread, the poor widow did not give him bread made from leftover flour but instead made bread with flour that could only provide one meal. Because of this, we must understand that afterward, the widow of Zarephath did not have to worry about food.

While Elijah stayed at the widow's house, her son, who was seriously ill, died, and the widow held the child and appealed to Elijah. Hearing the widow's earnest plea, Elijah prayed before heaven, and the dead child came back to life. On Mount Carmel, he killed over 800 prophets of Baal and Asherah, which was a great battle to distinguish between false gods and the true God.

In this context, Elijah realized that God had called him because He loved the nation. He understood that God's calling was to fight on His behalf against the enemies. He was called to represent the nation and to fight against the prophets of Baal and Asherah as a responsible leader. When heaven sent down fire to consume the drenched altar, Elijah killed the 800 prophets of Baal and Asherah. After this event, seeing the nation of Israel suffering from famine and starvation, Elijah climbed to the top of Mount Carmel and earnestly pleaded with heaven seven times, risking his life. Then, before King Ahab returned, rain began to fall.

Through this history, King Ahab and the people of Israel came to know the living God and realized that the Baal they served was a false god, and they should repent and follow Elijah. Yet, they did not follow Elijah. Ahab went among the crowd and reported the events in detail to Jezebel. Then Jezebel sent a message to Elijah saying, "You will be like the prophets of Baal whom you killed."

In response, Elijah crossed the borders of Israel and reached Beersheba in Judah, leaving his servant there and going further into the wilderness for a day's journey. Under a broom tree, he built an altar before heaven and prayed.

Although he had hoped to escape to Judah beyond the borders of Israel, his way was blocked. Knowing that he was chosen to save Israel, Elijah had worked hard through numerous adversities and battles, yet he could not achieve the desired results. So, having fled to Judah but finding his way blocked, Elijah knelt down and said, "Heaven, you have killed all your prophets, and you have sent me, but I cannot find anyone who seeks you or has a heart to face you, and they are trying to capture me. I can go no further. Please let me die."

"Father! I am the only one left."
We must understand that heaven, witnessing Elijah, who had worked hard to fulfill the purpose for which God had called him and led the nation, crying out in a sorrowful place, "Father, I am the only one left!" felt even greater sorrow.

Heaven regarded Elijah, who was being pursued and oppressed, as more precious than the many people of Israel and placed a greater hope in him than the hope He had for the land of Israel. We should reflect on Elijah, who, exhausted and with hope cut off, pleaded for a final decision in the wilderness where he could not find a way forward. Furthermore, we must recognize God, who led the nation of Israel, who worked hard to find and establish Elijah, and who helped him through various miracles when he was in distress, holding him from his home. Here, you must understand that heaven's heart toward Elijah became filled with sorrow.

Realizing that he could not stay in Judah, Elijah fled to Mount Horeb, near Sinai, where God had blessed the Israelites when they came out of Egypt. God knew that Elijah would have to cross the borders and understood that the way he was fleeing was long and that he had no friends or sympathizers along the way. Therefore, God sent an angel to Elijah, who was sleeping under the broom tree, telling him to eat bread baked on hot coals and drink a jar of water.

After eating, Elijah regained his strength and had to run toward Israel, the land of sorrow, with the sorrow of heaven and the sorrow of his nation, and with a desire for revenge against his enemies. However, he fled in the opposite direction toward Mount Horeb.

After walking for 40 days and nights, Elijah, who went to a cave on Mount Horeb to sleep, found himself in a pitiful state, like a defeated soldier. After he had deviated from the path led by God and was sleeping in a cave for his own safety, heaven sought him again. When God asked Elijah, "What are you doing here, Elijah?" he replied, "I have been very zealous for the Lord God Almighty. The Israelites have rejected your covenant, torn down your altars, and put your prophets to death with the sword. I am the only one left, and now they are trying to kill me too." 

However, God did not directly appear before Elijah. Instead, He showed His presence through a strong wind, an earthquake, and a fire. Afterward, in the stillness, God appeared and called Elijah again. Elijah answered, "Father, all your prophets have been killed by their hands, and I am the only one left. I cannot go on. What shall I do in this situation?" But God said again, "Though Israel is under Ahab's control, there are still 7,000 who have not bowed to Baal. What will you do with them?" 

This was heaven's sorrowful heart toward Elijah regarding the 7,000 who were suffering under King Ahab and who had not bowed to Baal. 

Here, Elijah resolved again to return to Damascus according to heaven's command, anointing Hazael and Jehu as kings and anointing Elisha as a prophet to succeed him.

As Elijah turned his steps, he realized that heaven cared for the remaining 7,000 who had not bowed to Baal, and he made a new resolution.

In the same way, all those who are facing the will of providence today are walking the path of labor. They are walking the path of tears. They are carrying the cross on their backs and walking the path of oppression. So, who is the cause of this sorrow, grief, and injustice? It was for the nation. Furthermore, it was because of Satan, the enemy of God for 6,000 years.

We must understand that the reason for the sorrow and suffering that floods in and the storms of persecution that sweep in is to save the nation and to liberate heaven. However, even those who face the will of heaven find it difficult to feel such a heart of God.

Even on the cross, Jesus cared for heaven and loved his enemies.
Jesus was pursued by the church and by his nation. He was seen as a heretic by the church and as a destroyer of the law. He was pursued by his own people and was cast out of his home. He was also pursued by John the Baptist and his followers. He went into the wilderness, but there he was also pursued by Satan. It did not end there. Eventually, the whole world was mobilized to drive him to the cross, to Golgotha.

Yet, Jesus wept for the nation that branded him a traitor. Although Jesus was treated as a heretic by the Jewish community, he shed more tears for them than any priest in Israel. No one in that era stood by his side, yet Jesus was a friend of that time. Though he was branded a traitor by his nation, he was a loyal subject of the nation, and though he was branded a heretic by the church, he was a loyal subject of the church.

What kind of steps did he take? They were the steps of one torn, oppressed, and crushed, bearing the cross. Was that the only path? He also faced situations where reckless villains raised whips against him. If Jesus had been like Elijah in such a situation, he would have prayed again, "Father, I am the only one left."

However, when Jesus prayed in the Garden of Gethsemane, leaving three disciples behind, he said, "My Father, if it is possible, may this cup be taken from me. Yet not as I will, but as you will." (Matthew 26:39) This is what makes him great. He understood that his own situation was that he was the sacrifice for his nation, for humanity, and for the divine order.

Knowing this, Jesus was not only concerned about his own sorrow but was even more concerned about how great heaven's sorrow must be. Although he appeared for the nation, he was aware of the sorrow of heaven as he was betrayed by his nation. Jesus was the prince of heaven, the lord of all.
The main character of the warning was the Messiah. How could such a Jesus, destined for the tragic fate of the cross, lament? He could have mobilized the entire universe to lament, but because he felt that he could not lament himself, he thought it was shameful to stand in that position. Jesus, who had the responsibility to unite the church and the nation to build the kingdom of heaven and to present the world to the Father, did not feel any resentment when he had to walk the path of the cross without fulfilling that responsibility. His prayer, "Let this cup pass from me," was not because he was sorrowful about his own death. He prayed that way because he knew that the sorrow of the nation and the sorrow of heaven would be compounded by his own death.

Jesus knew that if he fell on the cross, the burden of the cross would remain for future generations of humanity, and that the history of sorrow would not end because of it. He knew that the path of Golgotha would not end. He knew that the path of death would not end. And he knew that if he walked the path of Golgotha, those who followed him would also have to walk that path. Jesus knew that there would be a path even more difficult than the cross remaining. 

Even when nails were driven into his hands and feet, and his side was pierced with a spear, causing him to bleed, Jesus knew that this would not stop with him, yet he still proclaimed to heaven, "It is finished." That statement did not mean that the path of the cross was completely over in the human world. It meant that the heartfelt appeal of those who wept and worried for the cross had reached heaven. You must understand that Jesus bore all the wrongs that countless prophets and saints had committed before heaven, and he was offered to heaven as a living sacrifice to comfort it.

Then, what was God's heart like towards Jesus? When he looked at the dying Jesus, crossing over the hill of the cross while worrying about heaven, if there was any resentment in the human world, it could not be greater than that. If there was any resentment in the 4,000 years of heavenly history, it could not be greater than that. 

However, as Jesus was dying, he said, "Father, forgive them, for they do not know what they are doing." God had the desire to judge immediately, even more than in the days of Noah, but because Jesus held on to the nation, held on to the church, and held on to the cross while dying, God could not abandon humanity and has been holding on to them. This emotional connection has been maintained with future humanity and the remaining Israelite nation, which is why God cannot abandon the betraying future humanity and continues to hold on to them. 

We must understand the heart of heaven towards Elijah. Those of us born in later generations must now understand this heavenly heart. Jesus longed to face heaven with this heart and hoped to live such a life. We, who are the descendants of Jesus, the heirs of Jesus, and those who should inherit Jesus' achievements, must become a group that can boast of being the substance of glory before heaven. Standing today with this mission and responsibility before heavenly expectations, we must think about what we should seek, what we should feel, and what we should do.

Now, what else should we think about? Since we have been told to become friends of Jesus and brides of Jesus, we must think about becoming such people. Furthermore, we must resolve the historical grievances that our ancestors had before heaven. Thus, we must not leave behind the lament of death for future generations. We must not leave the path of struggle as the Golgotha of death but must leave it as the Golgotha of victory. You must understand that heaven is looking for those who can take on such responsibilities.

If the mission of the end times lies with the believers, then we must understand the sad heart of heaven that faced Noah's family and the heart of Jesus. When Noah, who was established before heaven, after 120 years of labor, was spared from the flood judgment, heaven wanted to resolve all the grievances through the remaining eight members of Noah's family. However, due to Ham's mistake, the condition for lamentation remained, and we must be those who can understand and resolve the sorrow of Noah's family again.

Abraham had to offer his son Isaac as a sacrifice due to a mistake with the offering, and his descendants had to leave the land of Canaan and enter Egypt, enduring 400 years of hardship. Heaven raised Moses to return the Israelite nation to the welfare of Canaan, but during that process, the Israelite nation betrayed heaven multiple times. Since then, many of our ancestors have come forth with their intentions, but there has been no group that has received praise and blessings from heaven saying, "Yes, you have fulfilled my will. You have accomplished my desires."

You must understand the heart of heaven, which has been filled with sorrow due to our ancestors. Even if we stand in a position like Elijah, who faced persecution and oppression before King Ahab, we must not lament our own situation but must hold on to God and move forward. 

If Elijah had held the same heart that Jesus had in Gethsemane and on Golgotha, and if he had established a connection with heaven, heaven would have resolved a portion of the historical sorrow there. However, because he could not do so, the sorrow of heaven extended to Jesus. 

Yet, we know that because of Jesus' death, this intention has not been resolved and continues to this day. 

Today’s Elijah
When we look at the phenomena occurring in this world today, they are comparable to what happened in the days of King Ahab in ancient Israel. What is idolatry? It is abandoning heaven and worshiping something else, elevating that above God. Yet, we must recognize that countless people today are unknowingly under the idol of civilization. 

At such a time, if there is someone who has the heart of Elijah, who looked at King Ahab and felt the sorrowful heart of heaven, then that person must be able to comfort heaven with the same heart as Elijah and pray, "Please raise us as beloved sons and daughters who can embrace this land in the Father's bosom." They must have a heart that can look at this era with a greater sense of indignation than Elijah. 

If such a group does not exist, then even if I am humble, I must recognize that our ancestors upheld heaven's will, established the path of heavenly principles, and that God's work remains. Even if I think of myself as lacking, I must not consider myself insufficient but must become a group that builds altars and sheds tears in secret. If such a group does not appear on this earth, we will not be able to prevent the ultimate shape of this world from coming to an end.

King Ahab betrayed heaven and toyed with the Israelite nation, but that was a national issue. However, today, people globally are idolizing materialism and becoming slaves to civilization, not knowing where the center of their life is or what direction and position they should go, struggling without being able to find heaven. This group is like those who were captured by King Ahab in the past.

Before us today lies the global judgment of God. Just as there was judgment before King Ahab and the Israelite nation, we know that there will be a day of judgment when we must break the bundle of idols in the end times. At such a time, have you ever thought, even in your dreams, that heaven is looking at you with a heart more sorrowful than that which faced Elijah? If you have not, then you must reflect.

The Israelite nation centered around King Ahab should have faced heaven with the heart that whether they lived or died, they were the temple, and they should have worked to inherit heaven's tradition and become heaven's kin. However, because they could not do so, the Israelite nation centered around King Ahab ended in bloody battles, and we understand that this historical reality is being re-presented in today's era.

The world is one thing, but we must look at this era and understand our nation. We are the sons and daughters of Korea. We are the bloodline of Korea, inheriting the blood and flesh from our ancestors. We must recognize that there have been many loyal patriots who bled and shed tears for the country, for the nation, and to bring a bright morning for the future of the nation. We must understand that we have gone through a tragic environment of sorrow and tragedy that no other nation has experienced, and at every moment, countless loyal patriots have walked the path of blood.

Having inherited this historical tradition, we must possess a heavenly principle that transcends human principles, push aside the civilization of this world that is like the idols of King Ahab's era, and ask who will build the new Jerusalem temple where heaven can reign. 

Now we must broaden our hearts. We must be able to mourn for the nation more than for ourselves, to mourn for humanity, and to mourn for God and heaven and earth. 

Where will the protagonists appear who can embrace the nation that is sighing under the fallen realm and weep on behalf of heaven? If the King of Kings, the Lord, descends upon this earth, he will undoubtedly come with a global ideology and will come to establish a mental connection with humanity as a global leader. 

However, if you do not think about such things today, the Lord cannot establish any relationship with you. Even if the Lord comes to rule with such an ideology, if you do not dream of or think about that world, you cannot establish any connection with it. You are in a position where you must at least think about it, worry about it, and fantasize about it.

Have you ever worried about individuals? Have you ever worried about families that are groaning in misery? Have you ever worried about any society or nation? If you find yourself in a position where you have not, you must expose your identity as a sinner before the cosmic history and have a heart to repent before heaven. 

If you do not even have such a heart, what will happen to this nation? Although the Korean people take pride in their 5,000-year history, having gone through the providential history of God and the history of suffering, if there is nothing, what can we contribute within world history, or within the realm of world civilization, or within the providential realm of God?

Even if we have something to boast about, if it cannot establish a heavenly and divine connection, it will only serve to increase heaven's sorrow. 

The Master of History
History has been made by those who have been oppressed and trampled upon. The main characters of history have been created by such people. Those who lived in high places, enjoying luxury and feasting, did not create any main characters. It is those who have been in the oppressed, trampled, and pitiful positions who have emerged. They are the ones who have walked the path of tears with every step.

When a nation is corrupt and the world is in chaos, those who hold the world and weep on behalf of heaven are the global heirs of Elijah. Such people can stand before heaven on behalf of the Israelite people that Elijah was concerned about. 

If Elijah says, "I am Elijah, and I am me," he will perish. We must be those who can weep and feel sorrow when heaven weeps and is sad. 

Heaven is not merely a being of words. God is a God of words, substance, heart, and love. Yet, we have become a people who do not even know the words. We do not know what the body is. We do not know what our own hearts are like. We do not know what the love of heaven that heaven claims is. 

Dear ones! How can you explain what God's love is? How can you explain what the heart is? How can you explain what your own existence is? What can you explain about what you say? There is nothing. There is none.

Today, people boast of their own excellence. But how long can they boast of that? How many centuries did the names that were boasted of in past eras last? Therefore, if there is anything to boast about in humanity, it is to walk the path that others cannot walk. Such a nation will not perish.

It is not those who have walked the common path of all nations that have saved the nation and the world, but those who have walked the path that others could not walk. The path of Christianity has been such a path. 

Today, the world of Christianity must lament. If they believe in God and know the death of Jesus on the cross, and if they understand the history of the Holy Spirit that has labored for 2,000 years since Jesus, they cannot sleep peacefully when looking at the reality of Christianity today. 

The Jews of Jesus' time enjoyed going to church more than the churchgoers of this era. They had better ceremonies and forms than the churches of this era. It was not that there were no words, nor that there was no history, nor that there were no conditions to boast about. However, the reason they could not boast of such Judaism before heaven was that they did not know heaven's new providence.

Therefore, Jesus hopes that today’s Christians will recall his death and think, "The heart of Jesus is my heart, and the body of Jesus that was nailed on Calvary is my body." He longs for such friends. He also longs for the bride he could not speak of while dying, the one he yearned for deeply in his heart. Only on the day he meets that bride can he open his heart and speak of his entire life, and he can express the sorrow of God's inner heart that has worked for 6,000 years. The content will differ from the words in the Bible.

If the sorrow of Jesus and the sorrow of God are before your beloved sons and daughters, what will you do? If it is before your beloved parents, what will you do?

The time is flowing increasingly towards the final resolution. History is flowing, religion is flowing, and the Lord is flowing. To solve these problems, there is fighting here and fighting there, sighing here and sighing there.

In this time of confusion, when it is hard to believe and hard to grasp, just as Elijah appeared and expressed a new heart, there must be some new voice that expresses the heart of heaven that has not been found in history, and you must think about that.

The Attitude of Faithful People in This Era
The Lord and ideology are stimulating you at every moment today. This is a peculiar time. The fear of history is driving you away, but who will personally sing the song of victory against that fear? There is no one.

So where will this history go? Death is looming, but where will the cries for new hope and new liberation come from? They must come out soon, but that is the problem.

Now, something new that you cannot imagine must emerge. Something that you cannot even think of in your dreams must come forth.
This era is a time of religious conflict. In the future, the struggles of nations, ethnicities, and ideologies, as well as religious conflicts, will all pass. What will remain is the struggle of the heart. Therefore, even if your heart is swept away by something you cannot understand, you must be able to overcome it. That time has come.

Although many people live in this world, when viewed from the vertical relationship with God, there is no relationship with you at all. You may think that the 30 million people of your nation are inextricably linked to you, but when centered on the vertical relationship with God, there is no relationship at all.

On the top of Mount Carmel, Elijah cried out, "O God, am I the only one left?" This cry should not only be Elijah's but should also be the cry of the multitude that must be judged in this end time. 

Are you not in such a position? Who guarantees your life? Not your parents, not your beloved spouse, not your children, not your nation, nor any ideology. Think about yourselves who respect such a life. Do not boast of your empty self that cannot clarify its identity as it is swept into an endless vortex.

Today, humanity must go through the history of Elijah's struggle on Mount Carmel. Like Elijah, who appealed to heaven saying, "Am I the only one left?" we must learn to appeal to heaven. If you realize that no ideology can save you as you stand at the endpoint of history, you must raise your head high toward heaven. You should aspire to where your heart is directed, where your heart can be liberated. You need to be filled with such desires, and life among us must be vibrant, and we must recognize that there is something left for us to do.

Is there a group today that can say, "It is finished," as Jesus did on Mount Calvary? We must become a group that can say, "O God, am I the only one left?" That time is approaching you.

Knowing that the providence to start a new history is before you, based on a day of judgment, you should be able to say, "Am I the only one left?" Why? Why? Why?

Today, we cannot believe in any religion, any ideology, any family, relatives, or teachers, nor any way. We are in a position where we cannot believe in any of these things. You are in a position where you can only say to heaven, "Am I the only one left?" The attitude you must take in such a position is to cry out to heaven, "Am I the only one left?" You must cry out like this from your heart.

Now, each of you must go through the process of struggle. There is a heavenly purpose to fulfill, a nation to find, and a denomination to be separated. Those on God's side must be mobilized for that purpose.

**Life's Path to Be Walked with Hope**

**Life's Path to Be Walked with Hope**

**<Message>** The title I would like to share with you for a moment is "Life's Path to Be Walked with Hope." I will speak for a moment with this title.

**Humans Who Have Lost Hope**  
Due to the fall of humanity, we have not been able to fulfill the true hope of heaven and have lived until now losing the hope that heaven had granted. Therefore, we cannot deny that from the day we were born until the day we die, we are destined to seek the path of true hope. 

God said to Adam and Eve before the fall, "Be fruitful and multiply and subdue the earth." This was granting Adam and Eve a standard of hope, but because the progenitors of humanity fell, they lost the standard of hope that heaven had granted, and furthermore, they lost the happiness of the garden where they could receive God's love and live forever, that is, the world of the overall ideal. 

Humans who have lost the path of true hope have been walking the path of various twists and struggles since they were born on this earth to find the hope they have lost. We are experiencing this fact deeply. 

Until now, humans have not realized that they have become beings without hope, but through God's compassionate grace, a promise of hope has been established for humanity. This is a hope that has been set before humans.
a shining example of hope and faith. 

Above all, it is a fortunate thing, and if it is a blessing, it is a blessing beyond measure. 
Before Jesus came, humanity could not live as beings who could sing of eternal life within the infinite realm of hope centered on the eternal heaven. Therefore, heaven, seeing that humans could not live within such a realm of hope, worked tirelessly to allow humanity to transcend their miserable living conditions and carve out a path of hope. We know this well. 
Among those born on this earth, there are people who live with hope and those who do not. However, hope can be divided into two types: hope centered on humanity and hope centered on heaven. 
From the day we are born, we grow up believing that our mother’s embrace is the best thing for us, but as we grow, we leave our mother’s arms, and then we make friends, believing that friends are the best, but we eventually part from them as well. 
Thus, as humans grow, they come to realize that even beloved parents cannot encompass all their hopes, that even beloved spouses cannot encompass all their hopes, and further, that even beloved children cannot encompass all their hopes. 
Humans have many hopes, but they come to understand that the heart that hopes can eventually fade away. 
They may have hopes for family, for their nation, and even for the world, but as they age, it is a fact that their hearts of hope gradually weaken. Among those living on this earth, we know that there are not many who boast of their hopes as their entire hope and live with a firm belief that they cannot live without it, even if it means losing their lives. Humans live like this and ultimately face the fate of having to confront death. 
Hope that can overcome death
Throughout their lives, humans hold various hopes, but in the end, they encounter death and leave behind all the hopes they once held. They wish to live today and hope to live tomorrow, wandering in search of new hopes, but when faced with death, they go on their final journey in despair without hope. We know this fact well. 
When viewed from a human-centered perspective, it may seem like they have hope, but they lack the hope that can overcome the peak of death. They are disappearing without having that hope. Will they consider this as the model of their lives and die? Or will they seek a hope that can laugh at and transcend death, enjoying that hope as they go on? I believe this is an important issue that people living on this earth must contemplate today. 
Today, all worldly matters pass away. Families pass away, nations pass away, and the world or any ideology passes away, but what must ultimately remain is a hope that can fight and win against death. If we do not have such hope, we could be considered losers in life. 
On the other hand, there are those who, from birth, reject all the hopes that the world desires, reject everything human in their lives, and live with a new hope from heaven, an eternal hope. 
Heaven has worked tirelessly to enable humans living centered on human hopes to have new hopes, to overcome the peak of death, and to live while yearning for the eternal world. Therefore, those who practice faith should not live with any hopes of this world but should hold onto hopes that can transcend even death and dream of the eternal world of hope. This is why we are currently engaged in our faith life. 
The reason Jesus could overcome all suffering and death
Jesus was someone who rejected all earthly hopes that humans held from a young age. From his early years, he abandoned his family, his environment, his denomination, and even his nation, living with a firm belief and hope in heaven that no one could shake. The hope he held in his young heart was an unwavering hope that could overcome any difficult circumstance, and he steadily ran his course. 
When Jesus was twelve years old, he went to the Jerusalem temple with his parents. However, his parents returned home first, leaving Jesus alone there. Later, when his parents came looking for him, Jesus asked, “Why were you searching for me? Didn’t you know I had to be in my Father’s house?” (Luke 2:49), rebuking his parents instead. This shows that Jesus held only hope for his Father. 
We must also recognize that as Jesus matured, he worked tirelessly to organize his surrounding environment. Furthermore, Jesus had a conviction for heaven. The conviction he had was one that no one else possessed. Because Jesus had the belief that he would build a new kingdom of hope, a new world of hope, he faced many difficulties on his path, but those difficulties could not remove the hope he held. 
During his earthly life, Jesus worked as a carpenter in Joseph's household, and despite being in an unfree environment and feeling internal struggles, he did not retreat but overcame that situation. We know that he fought with a heart devoted to heaven and a sincere hope. 
Thus, when he turned thirty, he set his mind, made new resolutions, and embarked on a path of adventure, but those around him did not support his journey. His family persecuted him, the church persecuted him, and society persecuted him. No one turned back to look at Jesus. Even in a position where he had no choice but to despair, he overcame those difficulties because he had a conviction that no one else possessed, that is, a single hope. We must recognize that Jesus, holding such hope and conviction, overcame all difficulties and organized every environment. 
He appointed twelve disciples, but they were also pushed around. However, the more he was pushed around, the more he longed for his Father’s kingdom. It was the heart of the Father. Although Jesus faced many battles and difficulties, those could not extinguish the hope he held. 
From birth, Jesus clung to hope and fought until the end. Even when his denomination and nation betrayed him, and even his disciples betrayed him, he did not abandon hope, and even knowing that he would be crucified, he held onto hope and did not retreat. 
Certainly, the life he lived was precious, but his hope for eternal life after death was greater, which is why he could bravely walk the path of the cross. We know well that Jesus bore witness to the entirety of hope before heaven and earth through death. On the final path to the cross, he prayed, “If it is possible, may this cup be taken from me. Yet not as I will, but as you will.” (Matthew 26:39). In that moment, the more the fear of death swept over him, the more he felt that the day of hope was drawing near. 
After overcoming physical death, he felt that a new world of hope would unfold before him and longed for that world. Because he hoped and longed to resurrect in a body of eternal freedom after physical death, we know that he could wear the glory of resurrection after death. 
Awareness and conviction about hope
In the same way, today’s believers must understand how much more precious it is to hold onto a hope that can remain in the eternal world than to cling to any hope that can remain on this earth. Today, many Christian believers often overlook the eternal hope that should be prioritized in their faith life. However, we must become people who can hold onto the hope that connects us to the eternal world and be willing to sacrifice everything for that hope. Only then can we truly become the ultimate victors. 
Not only Jesus but all the prophets of the past walked the path of death without concern. They did not care about being ridiculed by everyone. They did not care about persecution. The reason they walked through all those difficult paths was that they had an eternal hope that could not be exchanged for anything. They had a fervent hope that was not worldly but connected to their hearts through the eternal heaven, which is why they did not care about the path of death, the path of persecution, or the path of hardship. 
Therefore, today, we believers must have hearts burning with hope. And we should not believe only in the hope that will be realized after death. We must be people who can bring that hope into reality and fight, prepared to face death and achieve victory. If there are such people, they can be seen as truly victorious believers, not those who possess any hope of this world but those who possess eternal hope. 
If such hope is false, then all the facts that heaven has emphasized for thousands of years for humans to have hope in heaven would be false, and heaven could be considered an infinitely false existence. It would be the ultimate deception of humanity. 
Humans have long yearned for good things in their hearts and sought better things. Throughout a long historical process, they have not forgotten heaven and have longed for it in their hearts while striving with their bodies. Heaven is something everyone must yearn for; it is a goal that all humanity should aspire to. That is why countless people have devoted their hearts and efforts to hope in heaven as the standard of hope. 
Therefore, the question now is whether your yearning for heaven is giving you the shock to break through your circumstances. If the frequency of such shocks to yourself decreases, you must realize that you will inevitably collapse when faced with death. 
That is why today, we must abandon all worldly hopes and hold onto the hope of the eternal heaven. We must have a firm conviction that can push away all hopes centered on the world. If there is no such conviction, your faith life cannot be considered normal. 
No one can guarantee that they will not walk the path of suffering, persecution, or even death. Therefore, as you seek eternal hope, you must have a firm conviction that you cannot exchange this hope for any internal or external difficulties that may arise. 
Jesus did not abandon the hope he held since childhood, even in the midst of struggles, even when he fell, and even after he resurrected. Because he fought while holding onto the hope he had from a young age, he was able to carve out a path of hope for all humanity to live and became the central being of hope that all could rely on. 
So, what should you hope for today? You should have the hope of wanting to overcome the peak of death and attain the glory of resurrection, and after attaining the glory of resurrection, you should desire to become true sons and daughters of God. Then, you should hope to dwell with God forever, live for God forever, and seek God’s true love. Until these hopes are fulfilled, even if there is an infinite path of the cross, even if infinite suffering sweeps over you, even if there are countless peaks of difficulties, you must not retreat. Naturally, you should know that you will face such suffering and become someone with a firm hope who can push through with your body. If you do not become such a person, you must realize that you cannot be the ultimate victor. 
Hope and practical life
After Jesus came and went, the twelve apostles also faced similar challenges. They entered Rome and suffered immense abuse. They were crucified, sawed in half, or thrown into pots of oil to die. Yet, they did not abandon their hope. Their hope was stronger than death, stronger than any suffering, and stronger than any weapon. It was stronger than any authority and stronger than anything the world could boast of. We know that Christianity was established on the foundation of such strong hope. 
Today, we too are in a position where we must hold onto new hope and establish our intentions globally. If we admit this, we must recognize that the hope we hold must possess a power stronger than any other force. Even if death comes, we must have the power to overcome it, and even if everything disappears, we must have the power to transcend it. Only by becoming the protagonist of such unwavering hope can you stand before heaven. 
Until now, many have boasted of their faith, but we have often seen those who boasted disappear in an instant. No matter how much one boasts of their faith, if they cannot stand as a central being of victorious hope who has overcome the final peak of death, they will ultimately become a loser in life. 
If we can become people who hold onto a hope that cannot be exchanged for anything, a hope more precious than our own lives, and dedicate ourselves to heaven, then through that church and nation, a new hope will emerge on this land where hope is absent, and those who have wandered without finding hope will find new hope through them. 
Therefore, each of you who have set out to find a new path must have a hope that you cannot help but boast about to anyone, a hope that you cannot help but boast about before all people, and an eternal, unchanging hope that you cannot help but boast about even in the face of any fear or death. You must become someone who can bravely and joyfully overcome any difficult circumstances under the conviction that you have such hope. If you become such a person, you will not be someone who possesses the joys of this world but someone who possesses the joys of the eternal heaven. The life found in such a pursuit is not a life that lives and dies in this world but a life that can live forever. Furthermore, if there is someone seeking such hope, they will be someone who can live forever in the love of God, not in the love that humanity cries out for. Additionally, if someone has found such hope, they will be the sons and daughters of the eternal Father, shining before all people.
